### Post by Mazza558 on 2008-03-31
April 2008 Desktops - Posting Guidelines

* Stay within the board rules, no matter how hot you may believe the wallpaper/screen shot to be.

* If you are going to quote, there isn't a need to quote an img-embeded picture - Just don't do it. Please just reference the post by page number/page link/etc.

* Off Topic Posts will be edited or removed.

* The desktops thread is not to be used as a means to post explicit or suggestive, and provocative images (they must be safe for your kids and/or boss to see). Please help to keep the thread relevant and safe to browse for everyone.

* The moderators of this forum reserve the right to edit or remove your posts as necessary so they may comply with our Community Rule set.

* Please use reduced-size thumbnails, where possible, out of respect for people running on lower bandwidth or screen resolutions.

*To avoid having users having to ask you for them. we request that you format your posts in the following order:

Themes: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).

Wallpaper: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).

Icons: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).

Programs: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).

Important Note: Any image posted that is over 800 x 600 will be removed! Use a thumbnail or use a text link to your image. If your image is removed, this is why.

.conkyrc (It wouldn't let me upload it as an attachment :/)
```
# UBUNTU-CONKY
# A comprehensive conky script, configured for use on
# Ubuntu / Debian Gnome, without the need for any external scripts.
#
# Based on conky-jc and the default .conkyrc.
# INCLUDES:
# - tail of /var/log/messages 
# - netstat connections to your computer
#
# -- Pengo (conky@pengo.us)
#

# Create own window instead of using desktop (required in nautilus)
own_window yes
own_window_type override
own_window_transparent yes
own_window_hints undecorated,below,sticky,skip_taskbar,skip_pager

# Use double buffering (reduces flicker, may not work for everyone)
double_buffer yes

# fiddle with window
use_spacer yes
use_xft yes
xftfont Purisa:size=8
xftalpha 0.8


# Update interval in seconds
update_interval 0.50

# Minimum size of text area
# minimum_size 250 5

# Draw shades?
draw_shades no

# Text stuff
draw_outline no # amplifies text if yes
draw_borders no
#font -*-gentium-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*
uppercase no # set to yes if you want all text to be in uppercase

# Stippled borders?
stippled_borders 3

# border margins
border_margin 7

# border width
border_width 10

# Default colors and also border colors, grey90 == #e5e5e5
default_color grey

own_window_colour brown
own_window_transparent yes

# Text alignment, other possible values are commented
#alignment top_left
alignment top_right
#alignment bottom_left
#alignment bottom_right

# Gap between borders of screen and text
gap_x 10
gap_y 10

# stuff after 'TEXT' will be formatted on screen

TEXT
$color
${color orange}SYSTEM ${hr 2}$color
$nodename $sysname $kernel on $machine for $uptime

${color orange}DATE ${hr 2}$color
${execi 1 date}

${color orange}CPU ${hr 2}$color
${freq}MHz   Load: ${loadavg}   Temp: ${acpitemp}
$cpubar
${cpugraph 000000 ffffff}
NAME             PID       CPU%      MEM%
${top name 1} ${top pid 1}   ${top cpu 1}    ${top mem 1}
${top name 2} ${top pid 2}   ${top cpu 2}    ${top mem 2}
${top name 3} ${top pid 3}   ${top cpu 3}    ${top mem 3}
${top name 4} ${top pid 4}   ${top cpu 4}    ${top mem 4}

${color orange}MEMORY / DISK ${hr 2}$color
RAM:   $memperc%   ${membar 6}$color
Swap:  $swapperc%   ${swapbar 6}$color
HDD:  ${fs_free_perc /}%   ${fs_bar 6 /}$color 

${color orange}NETWORK (${addr eth0}) ${hr 2}$color
Down: $color${downspeed eth0} k/s ${alignr}Up: ${upspeed eth0} k/s
${downspeedgraph eth0 25,140 000000 ff0000} ${alignr}${upspeedgraph eth0 
25,140 000000 00ff00}$color
Total: ${totaldown eth0} ${alignr}Total: ${totalup eth0}
Inbound: ${tcp_portmon 1 32767 count} Outbound: ${tcp_portmon 32768 
61000 count}${alignr}Total: ${tcp_portmon 1 65535 count}

${color orange}BATTERY ${hr 2}$color
${execi 1 acpi}

${color orange}FORTUNE ${hr 2}$color
${execi 120 cowsay `fortune -s` | fold -w50}


```

#**********************************************************************
#
#    .twmrc

	"wmbattery"
}

#AppletRegion +300+50-300+0 North East 20 20 {

#NoDecorateTransients

{
	"VTWM Desktop"
	"VTWM Icon Manager"

#ShallowReliefWindowButton

}

{
    BorderColor "black"

    IconBorderColor "green"
    IconManagerForeground "black"
    IconManagerBackground "grey15"
    VirtualBackground "grey15"
}



#Button = KEYS : CONTEXT : FUNCTION
#----------------------------------
Button2 =      : root    : f.menu "twm menu"
Button1 =  c   : root    : f.menu "rootmenu"
Button1 =  m   : title   : f.menu "Frame"
Button3 =      : frame   : f.menu "Frame"

Button1 =  c   : title   : f.move
Button2 =      : frame   : f.move
Button2 =  c s : title   : f.forcemove
Button2 =  c   : title   : f.resize
Button2 =  c   : frame   : f.resize
Button1 =      : title   : f.zoom
Button1 =  c   : frame   : f.zoom
Button1 =      : title   : f.raise
Button1 =      : frame   : f.raise
Button1 =  s   : title   : f.lower
Button1 =  s   : frame   : f.lower
Button2 =      : icon    : f.move


#KEY 	= KEYS : CONTEXT : FUNCTION
#----------------------------------
"KP_Add"=      : window  :f.raiselower
"F5"    =      : window  :f.raiselower
"L5"	=      : window  :f.raiselower
"KP_Enter"=    : window  :f.iconify
"L7"	=      : window  :f.iconify
"F7"	=      : window  :f.iconify
"KP_Enter"=    : icon    :f.deiconify
"L7"    =      : icon    :f.deiconify
"F7"    =      : icon    :f.deiconify
"Right" =    m : all     :f.downiconmgr

"Pause"	=  m s : all	 :!"lockscreen &"

"KP_1"	=    s : all	 :f.warpto "CATFISH"

"KP_Insert" = m : all    :!"sh -c 'if xmmsctrl playing; then xmmsctrl pause; else xmmsctrl play; fi'"

#"Left" = meta : all : f.exec "xmmsctrl prev"
#"Right" = meta : all : f.exec "sh -c 'if xmmsctrl playing; then if xmmsctrl paused; then xmmsctrl pause; else xmmsctrl next; fi; else xmmsctrl play; fi'"
#"Down" = meta : all : f.exec "sh -c 'if xmmsctrl playing; then if xmmsctrl paused; then xmmsctrl stop; else xmmsctrl pause; fi; else xmmsctrl play; fi'"

"KP_4" = m s c : all     :!"xmmsctrl prev"
"KP_6" = m s c : all     :!"xmmsctrl next"
"KP_2" = m s c : all     :!"xmmsctrl vol -10"

{

"Full Screen"           f.fullzoom

}

menu "twm menu"
{
"Window Ops"		f.title
"Refresh"		!"switcher -e 0; xrefresh"
"Focus on Root"		f.unfocus
"Re-read .twmrc"	f.twmrc
"Source something"	f.source "something"
"Hide Icon Manager"     f.hideiconmgr 
"Show Icon Manager"     f.showiconmgr 
"twm Version"		f.version
"(De)Iconify"           f.iconify
"Move Window"           f.move
"Resize Window"         f.resize
"Raise Window"          f.raise
"Lower Window"          f.lower
"Focus on Window"       f.focus
"Destroy Window"        f.destroy
"Exit TWM (only)"	f.quit
"Exit X Windows"	!"kill -TERM $XTOOLSPID"
}

```

### Post by spupy on 2008-03-31
I'm thinking of editing the ROX source code to make the icons on the desktop bigger - these are some delicious japanese-themed icons.

Programs you see are Rox Filer, Leafpad,  Firefox, aterm, conky.

I use the Tango icon set, with Yoritsuki Japanese icons set for some special folders.

GTK theme is Aurora Borealis edited for extra roundedness.

Fluxbox theme is created by me to fit with gtk (it's really just one gradient, this kind are my fluxbox themes :)).

Wallpaper is called ... "Stripes" by invaderjohn on deviantart.com

On the first image you see "TEH ZEN". My desktop looks like that after i start it.
Second screen demonstrates the gtk theme, you can also see the icons of some minimized windows, scattered around.
The last one is Rox boasting beautiful icons, conky running, and the ultimate fluxbox eyecandy - xcompmgr. :|

[**Click here for more screens**.]("http://vesso.marv.lafka.net/screens/screens19/") Go up one folder for big gallery of evolving desktop since 2006.

### Post by racoq on 2008-04-01
> **el mariachi said:**
> you're supposed to lie not mess with my eyes lololol

You can restore the default theme, at the end of the home page of ununtu forums (botom-left) there is a drop down that says, -- default style uf 2.5af (a = april, f = fools), change it to -- default style uf 2.5 and you are done

### Post by aidanr on 2008-04-01
> **lode said:**
> Could you please tell how to remove some of Sonata's tabs (you've only got Current, Library and Info -- I wonder where Playlists and Streams have gone to)?

With 1.4 onwards right click on the tabs to select which ones to hide/show. There's an old version in the repos 1.2 or something, you can get newer versions from [getdeb]("http://getdeb.net/search.php?keywords=sonata").

### Post by supersonicdarky on 2008-04-01
Without xgl xcompmgr messes up the window borders. I can't stand defects :P

```
#---------------------------------------------
# TTM CONFIG FILE
#
# colors: hex format
# booleans: 0 or 1 
# alpha: 0 to 100 percent
# font: [FAMILY-LIST] [STYLE-OPTIONS] [SIZE]
# panel_width: 0 == use full width
#---------------------------------------------

#---------------------------------------------
# FONT
#---------------------------------------------
font = ambitsek regular 8
font_color = #ffffff
font_alpha = 35
font_active_color = #ffffff
font_active_alpha = 75
font_shadow = 0

#---------------------------------------------
# TASKS
#---------------------------------------------
task_text_centered = 0
task_width = 110
task_margin = 3
task_padding = 5

#---------------------------------------------
# PANEL
#---------------------------------------------
panel_width = 0
panel_height = 24
panel_tasks_centered = 0

#---------------------------------------------
# ICON
#---------------------------------------------
icon = 1
icon_size = 16

#---------------------------------------------
# PANEL BACKGROUND
#---------------------------------------------
panel_background = 0
panel_background_color = #000000
panel_background_alpha = 25

#---------------------------------------------
# TASK BACKGROUND
#---------------------------------------------
task_background = 1
task_background_color = #ffffff
task_background_alpha = 50
task_active_background_color = #ffffff
task_active_background_alpha = 100
task_background_as_border = 1
```

although I can't get it to set the desired font.

### Post by What is in a name? on 2008-04-02
> **sujoy said:**
> hey guys, i am using xfce4 nowadays, but can seem to be able to remove the icons from the desktop right click menu. however i can remove the icons from the menu applet on the panel.

how do i remove the icons?

I believe it actually depends on the GTK theme you're using. I'm a Xfce user myself, and what I do is to go to the gtkrc file inside of the gtk-2.0 directory of the theme I'm currently using. After opening the gtkrc with, say, Gedit or Mousepad, you might find an option on the first lines of the document, saying "gtk-menu-images = 1". Switch the 1 to a 0 (zero). Save the gtkrc file and reload the theme. That should work.

---

### Post by Mateo on 2008-04-02
> **urukrama said:**
> What is that calendar/todo application (top right)? It looks interesting.

calcurse, a CLI calendar app.  It's pretty nice, for what it is.  one thing I like about it is how it can return your appointments from the command line.  for example doing this:

> calcurse -n | tr -d '\n'

will give me my next scheduled appointment.  i added this to my wmii config file, and now it will always show my next appointment (if in the same day) on the notification area.  Here is a screenshot. look in the bottom right, it's telling me to go to bed at a reasonable time tonight.

### Post by Ub1476 on 2008-04-03
Black-white icon theme. Will probably change or make custom, need more minimalistic and better app support (like Tango).. 

GTK2 theme is Clearlooks Dark Brave.

Wallpaper is Hardy-Simple Brave.

Emerald theme is Gommoso Brave Dark.

Removed all panels by adding this in Compiz-Fusion>General Options>Opacity>**(class=Gnome-panel) & !(type=Dialog)** with value 0.

Using gnome-do for opening apps. For notification-area, I just got to remember where certain apps I need to open/see info is placed..

Music player is MPD with Sonata.

### Post by cubekid on 2008-04-04
> **DrOlaf said:**
> That would make a great login screen. I know I should JFGI*, but does anyone know any good tutorials on how to create a new login screen?

*JFGI = Just Flipping well Google It

I don't know of any tutorials, but i've noticed that it's usually not that hard to tweak existing ones. All you really have to do is rename the picture you want as background.jpg, move it to the login screen folder, and then edit the rc file. At least for changing small things, it's usually pretty easy to do it this way.

### Post by klange on 2008-04-04
The Compiz Fusion Live CD theme work continues with this wallpaper featuring a not often seen Compiz Decorator icon (representing Emerald and the future decorator that's currently being worked on) and screenlet-based launcher set up (who needs Nautilus when you can draw your own dang icons?):

[[img]http://random.ogunderground.com/compiz/cftheme/thumbs/new_icons.png[/img]](http://random.ogunderground.com/compiz/cftheme/new_icons.png)
Other wallpapers are there for the Core icon and the Compiz Settings icon, the latter of which is shown as a launcher.
The icons launch CCSM, Emerald Theme Manager, and the C-F web site.

---

### Post by DrOlaf on 2008-04-04
> **cubekid said:**
> I don't know of any tutorials, but i've noticed that it's usually not that hard to tweak existing ones. All you really have to do is rename the picture you want as background.jpg, move it to the login screen folder, and then edit the rc file. At least for changing small things, it's usually pretty easy to do it this way.

> **uzusan said:**
> There is a tutorial on gnome art : [http://live.gnome.org/GnomeArt/Tutorials/GdmThemes](http://live.gnome.org/GnomeArt/Tutorials/GdmThemes)

Thanks for the heads up, guys. That was very straightforward.

There is nothing wrong with Mr Mark's post, picture, or link.

### Post by klange on 2008-04-05
> **Martje_001 said:**
> How did you make that 'photo' effect?
ImageMagick:
```
mogrify -format png -thumbnail 200 PATH_TO_IMAGE
rot=0
let "rot = $RANDOM % 20 - 10"
convert PATH_TO_IMAGE \
          -bordercolor white  -border 6 \
          -bordercolor grey60 -border 1 \
          -background  none   -rotate $rot \
          -background  black  \( +clone -shadow 60x4+4+4 \) +swap \
          -background  none   -flatten \
          -depth 8  -quality 95   PATH_TO_IMAGE
```
(Do it to a thumbnail, mine is in a script I wrote to automatically take a format a bunch of screenshots and which makes the thumbs itself)

---

I'm curious to know how to take a screenshot without X, I never did that.

---

### Post by jordanmthomas on 2008-04-07
> **ayoli said:**
> I'm curious to know how to take a screenshot without X, I never did that.
You can do it with fbgrab.
It's a little harder to do if you want to capture a running program (like htop) but you can still use fbgrab
In another tty, run
```
sleep 2; cp /dev/fb/0 fb.dump
```
(The sleep is to give you time to switch to the tty you want a screenshot of)
Then
```
 fbgrab -w 1280 -h 800 -b 32 -f fb.dump something.png
```
Obviously substitute proper numbers / filenames here.

If you just want to take a shot of the current tty (after running a program or something)
```
fbgrab somefile.png
```
is all you need.

---

### Post by ayoli on 2008-04-07

### Post by urukrama on 2008-04-07
> **PrimoTurbo said:**
> Also does anyone use sudo sudo shutdown -h now command to shutdown, it's odd but it doesn't work from openbox menu but works fine from terminal. Any clue what the problem is?

<item label="Reboot">
<action name=&#8221;Execute&#8221;> <execute>sudo shutdown -r now</execute> </action></item>
<item label=&#8221;Shut down&#8221;>
<action name=&#8221;Execute&#8221;> <execute>sudo shutdown -h now</execute> </action></item>

I use the same command, though not from the menu. I launch a script that gives me options (shutdown, reboot, log out) and asks for my confirmation (see [here]("http://urukrama.wordpress.com/2007/12/03/confirm-to-shut-down-reboot-or-log-out-in-openbox/") for more info).

Try using ```
sudo "shutdown -h now"
``` in your Openbox menu. Perhaps that works better.

**EDIT** (after reading kaivalagi's comment): I assumed you use shutdown without administrative privileges (because you have edited the sudoers file). If you don't, follow kaivalagi's advice.

---

### Post by kaivalagi on 2008-04-07
> **PrimoTurbo said:**
> [[IMG]http://img231.imageshack.us/img231/952/001march072008zo1.th.jpg[/IMG]](http://img231.imageshack.us/my.php?image=001march072008zo1.jpg)

A very default openbox setup, using a customized fbpanel.

Also does anyone use sudo sudo shutdown -h now command to shutdown, it's odd but it doesn't work from openbox menu but works fine from terminal. Any clue what the problem is?

<item label="Reboot">
<action name=”Execute”> <execute>sudo shutdown -r now</execute> </action></item>
<item label=”Shut down”>
<action name=”Execute”> <execute>sudo shutdown -h now</execute> </action></item>
> **urukrama said:**
> I use the same command, though not from the menu. I launch a script that gives me options (shutdown, reboot, log out) and asks for my confirmation (see [here]("http://urukrama.wordpress.com/2007/12/03/confirm-to-shut-down-reboot-or-log-out-in-openbox/") for more info).

Try using ```
sudo "shutdown -h now"
``` in your Openbox menu. Perhaps that works better.

Sudo will prompt for a password, and if you're doing this through a menu there is no ability to capture it unless you follow urukrama's webpage instructions, (hence why it works on the command line). Do you have gksudo installed? If you use this it will prompt graphically for a password.

i.e. 

```
gksudo shutdown -h now
```

Edit: Another option could be to use the following which will prompt for a decision (restart/shurtdown etc) but it requires gnome to be installed:

```
gnome-session-save --kill
```

### Post by Gigamo on 2008-04-07
! Breakage, how do you use terminus as the tty font? That's awesome!

---

### Post by Breakage on 2008-04-07
> **Gigamo said:**
> ! Breakage, how do you use terminus as the tty font? That's awesome!

Put it in your rc.conf like this: 

> CONSOLEFONT="ter-112n"

The top section of my rc.conf looks like this:

> 
LOCALE="en_GB.utf8"
HARDWARECLOCK="localtime"
USEDIRECTISA="yes"
TIMEZONE="Europe/London"
KEYMAP="uk"
CONSOLEFONT="ter-112n"
CONSOLEMAP=
USECOLOR="yes"


After there's a kernel update or you compile one then the font will start earlier after the arch logo disappears so it looks clean. :)

---

### Post by Gigamo on 2008-04-07
And you didnt do anything special but install the terminus-font package to get that to work, right?

---

### Post by Breakage on 2008-04-07
> **Gigamo said:**
> And you didnt do anything special but install the terminus-font package to get that to work, right?

Yep it's in the "terminus-font" package, no extra work needed. :D

So we need to host the pictures somewhere where the general public can see them.

---

### Post by mali2297 on 2008-04-08
> **urukrama said:**
> I tried this, but it doesn't work. I run Ubuntu Gutsy (command line install) and didn't have an /etc/rc.conf. I created one, and added what you mentioned, but nothing changed. I have the terminus font installed. Am I missing something?

In a tty, try
```

setfont Lat15-Terminus14

```
If it works, then you can put the line in ~/.profile or elsewhere.

The available fonts can be found in /usr/share/consolefonts.

---

### Post by Gigamo on 2008-04-08
> **urukrama said:**
> I tried this, but it doesn't work. I run Ubuntu Gutsy (command line install) and didn't have an /etc/rc.conf. I created one, and added what you mentioned, but nothing changed. I have the terminus font installed. Am I missing something?

Ah, the rc.conf is an Arch-only thing :) That's basically Arch's important configuration file where you specify the daemons/modules that get automatically loaded at boot, the locale, timezone, and apparently also the console font :)

consolechars -f Uni3-Terminus14

### Post by uzusan on 2008-04-09
A small change from yesterdays desktop.

I've created a script that will update the wallpaper to show the current date everyday by adding a small green overlay (attached) onto the wallpaper then setting that as wallpaper. Now i just need to update it each month.

[[IMG]http://tn3-2.deviantart.com/fs26/300W/f/2008/100/3/5/Auto_Updating_Wallpaper_by_uzusan.png[/IMG]]("http://fc06.deviantart.com/fs26/f/2008/100/3/5/Auto_Updating_Wallpaper_by_uzusan.png")


The script:

```
#!/bin/bash

D=$(date +%d)
let dlt=0


if [ "$D" -ge 1 ]; then
if [ "$D" -le 6 ]; then
let dlt=0
fi
fi

if [ "$D" -ge 7 ]; then
if [ "$D" -le 13 ]; then
let dlt=1
fi
fi

if [ "$D" -ge 14 ]; then
if [ "$D" -le 20 ]; then
let dlt=2
fi
fi

if [ "$D" -ge 21 ]; then
if [ "$D" -le 27 ]; then
let dlt=3
fi
fi

if [ "$D" -ge 28 ]; then
if [ "$D" -le 30 ]; then
let dlt=4
fi
fi

let "x = 126 + (dlt * 110)"
let "y = 195 + (dlt * 60)"

$(composite -compose multiply -geometry  +$x+$y today.png original.png ~/Pictures/wallpaper.png)
```

Then its called in autostart.sh using:

```
~/Pictures/wp.sh
hsetroot -center ~/Pictures/wallpaper.png &
```

### Post by uzusan on 2008-04-10
> **uzusan said:**
> A small change from yesterdays desktop.

I've created a script that will update the wallpaper to show the current date everyday by adding a small green overlay (attached) onto the wallpaper then setting that as wallpaper. Now i just need to update it each month.

[[IMG]http://tn3-2.deviantart.com/fs26/300W/f/2008/100/3/5/Auto_Updating_Wallpaper_by_uzusan.png[/IMG]]("http://fc06.deviantart.com/fs26/f/2008/100/3/5/Auto_Updating_Wallpaper_by_uzusan.png")


Made a few mistakes in the code. Now fixed:

```
#!/bin/bash

D=$(date +%d)
let dlt=0


if [ "$D" -ge 1 ]; then
if [ "$D" -le 6 ]; then
let dlt=0
let vdlt=0
fi
fi

if [ "$D" -ge 7 ]; then
if [ "$D" -le 13 ]; then
let dlt=1
let vdlt=7
fi
fi

if [ "$D" -ge 14 ]; then
if [ "$D" -le 20 ]; then
let dlt=2
let vdlt=14
fi
fi

if [ "$D" -ge 21 ]; then
if [ "$D" -le 27 ]; then
let dlt=3
let vdlt=21
fi
fi

if [ "$D" -ge 28 ]; then
if [ "$D" -le 30 ]; then
let dlt=4
let vdlt=28
fi
fi

let "y = 195 + (dlt * 60)"
let "dlt = dlt * ($D - $vdlt)"
let "x = 16 + (dlt * 110)"

$(composite -compose multiply -geometry  +$x+$y today.png original.png ~/Pictures/wallpaper.png)
```

---

And scroll down to where it says 
**GTK themes, fonts and icons in Openbox**

### Post by leftfield technology on 2008-04-14
Thankyou.. We were toying with KDE4 for a while. Loved the way it looked, but much preferred the feel and stability of the Ubuntu/Gnome setup.
So, rather than reinvent the wheel, we'd thought we'd combine the best bits of the distros/de's that we liked.
Hence, you end up with this Ubuntu/KDE4/Fedora inspired desktop.

The idea is is for it to be fresh enough to entice new users without being too much of a learning curve - eg. the windows-esque layout.

---

### Post by arbulus on 2008-04-14
Continuing my experimenting:

OpenBSD

This first screen shot is of the default install.  If you tell it to install X in the beginning, it gives you a VERY basic VERY simple looking FVWM setup.  Here's a shot of that:

[[IMG]http://img252.imageshack.us/img252/2076/fvwmopenbsdem2.th.png[/IMG]](http://img252.imageshack.us/my.php?image=fvwmopenbsdem2.png)

So, I decided to install KDE, since that was the only guide I could find for a DE installation. 

Just vanilla KDE.  The wallpaper is from Interfacelift.com.  I can't remember what it's called there, I renamed it when I downloaded it.   I can find a link if anyone wants it:

Clean:
[[IMG]http://img410.imageshack.us/img410/3676/openbsdkdecleantn8.th.jpg[/IMG]](http://img410.imageshack.us/my.php?image=openbsdkdecleantn8.jpg)

Dirty
[[IMG]http://img252.imageshack.us/img252/8057/openbsdkdedirtyam4.th.jpg[/IMG]](http://img252.imageshack.us/my.php?image=openbsdkdedirtyam4.jpg)

Based on what I've seen, OpenBSD isn't so hot of a desktop OS.  Excellent server OS, but it's far too difficult if not impossible to find things to work with on the desktop. That's not to say it can't be done, just far too difficult for my tastes.  But it was a snap to install.

This is a modified Wii-Black theme that uses the Enduro Black Smooth decorator. As you can see, between the 4th and 5th shots, I was addressing the corners of my GNOME panels so that they look like they are all one. In the last shot there, you can see I added a frame cube cap to make the cube look like an empty frame. Further changes to this theme are likely.

Don't forget, I have a whole GALLERY of screenshots [here.]("http://yaro.marupa.net/gallery/")

This took me all day to set up, and I think the effect is worth it.

### Post by What is in a name? on 2008-04-18
> **dbbolton said:**
> This screenshot and Raul's are some of the nicer KDE setups I've seen. Do you mind sharing the window theme, whatever the qt theme is called, and the icons :D

Thanks a lot! I consider my desktop is far from being perfect, but at least I'm feeling for the first time that I can use KDE for a really long time. I just didn't install any of the Kubuntu-specific packages. It's running wonderfully. I'm so happy indeed. And I'm finally coming to understand why Konqueror is such a great app. Look, you can browse your files, surf on the Net (with most sites, anyway), see your pictures, watch movies, play music, read PDF files, all inside of a single app, now THAT's awesome.

Anyway.
KDE has styles, which are a bit like what we'd call "engines" on the GTK universe (GNOME and Xfce, basically). And then you can configurate that style, that set of widgets, with your own definitions for size, shape, texture, etc., which is as close as you get to the idea of a "theme". Then you can also choose a specific colour scheme. That scheme can be used with any style, and all configurations at the style module can be applied under any color scheme (as long as the result isn't really awful in the aesthetical sense). That said, sometimes there are pre-packaged themes or suites with all those elements, which can be used on the K Theme Manager.

I'm using the Domino style: [http://www.kde-look.org/content/show.php/Domino+Deb+package+for+Kubuntu?content=74031](http://www.kde-look.org/content/show.php/Domino+Deb+package+for+Kubuntu?content=74031)
With the Béo theme (most precisely its Blue variant), for the Theme Manager: [http://www.kde-look.org/content/show.php/Béo?content=60013](http://www.kde-look.org/content/show.php/Béo?content=60013)
Raul kindly pointed me this link to a KDE3 port of the awesome Oxygen icons: [http://www.kde-look.org/content/show.php/Oxygen+Icons?content=74184](http://www.kde-look.org/content/show.php/Oxygen+Icons?content=74184)

The Domino style also happens to include a window decorator for KWin, which can also be configured. In my case, I just chose no specific colour for the borders, I made them thin too and I believe the buttons of the title are coloured with dark gray. 

I hope this helped you. Thanks again!

---

### Post by arbulus on 2008-04-21
I was intending to try out Gentoo next, but that didn't work out.  I went through the command-line install and it gave me a kernel panic after reboot.  Then I tried the live CD and the GUI installer and it failed twice.  I really don't know why, it wouldn't show me the installer log. 

So I tried out PCLinuxOS.
KDE 3.5
A very unattractive Domino Theme
Default icons
Wallpaper is "Scoreboard" from InterfaceLift

Clean
[[IMG]http://img329.imageshack.us/img329/1489/pclinuxoscleanxb8.th.jpg[/IMG]](http://img329.imageshack.us/my.php?image=pclinuxoscleanxb8.jpg)

Dirty
[[IMG]http://img329.imageshack.us/img329/5279/pclinuxosdirtysw4.th.jpg[/IMG]](http://img329.imageshack.us/my.php?image=pclinuxosdirtysw4.jpg)


PCLinuxOS is without a doubt one of the strangest distros I've ever tried.  I know it's marketed toward new users switching from Windows, but I don't think that works.  The install would probably be very intimidating for a new user.  It's unintuitive and the partitioner doesn't make much sense.

Secondly, it's an RPM based distro, but uses apt for its package management.  Which just seems incredibly confusing.

Thirdly, I don't spend much time in KDE, but I have to say that trying to theme KDE is almost impossible.  It is very very difficult, and PCLinuxOS's odd package management didn't make it any easier. Which I don't understand.  I've seen screenshots from people with very attractive KDE desktops, but I have never been able to successfully theme a KDE desktop.  Either themes won't install, won't change or I can't figure out how to change something. Themes almost always have to be compiled and leave you in a dependency nightmare (at least the ones I've tried).

Overall, I would not suggest PCLinuxOS to a new Linux user.

---

### Post by maniacmusician on 2008-04-24
I recently re-did the theme on my desktop, and tried my hand at a darker look. In the past, my attempts at creating a cohesive dark setup of themes have turned out pretty bad. But, I'm really pleased with this latest result.

I'm using Kubuntu Gutsy, with the Polyester style (flat buttons with light borders and shadowed, lowercased text; animated buttons to a lighter color; a colored, 18px KDE style scrollbar).

My window decorations are a modified version of Wombat Gray. I just changed a bunch of colors (but there were a lot of colors I had to change to get it to look this way), and there are also some other modifications that I'd made to the theme a long time ago. It's attached with this post.

I also made a custom color scheme for polyester, using the default Kubuntu color profile as the base (I called it DarkPolyester). This is also attached to the post. Please note that I ignored many elements of the color profile that didn't have any impact on me, such as a lot of the windeco options. Since I use emerald and not Kwin (in KDE3.5 at least), those had no bearing on me.  

I don't think I did anything else (well, I started using Stylish with firefox, but that's to be expected), so without further ado, the screenshot:

[[IMG]http://img87.imageshack.us/img87/5588/darkthemescreenshot1xe7.th.png[/IMG]](http://img87.imageshack.us/my.php?image=darkthemescreenshot1xe7.png)

I haven't really given any thought yet to the icon scheme, so that may seem a little out of place. Personally, I like the colorful contrast that the current one provides, but I'll probably replace it with a better fitting one within the next couple of weeks.

**Note:** The forum won't let me upload kcsrc (kde color profile) files, so I had to tar it. Just extract it and load it into the appropriate place to use it.

---

### Post by Saint Angeles on 2008-04-25
ok I spent all night and into the morning editing my SlickNess-Black theme. I took the taskbar button style from the Overglossed theme. I used GIMP to make it a cool aqua color. Then I took the scrollbars from the original Slickness theme and used GIMP to invert them to black and match the colors to the aqua-ish color from the panel. then I edited the menubar to add the aqua color.

I also took the shinier panel background from the SlickNess theme because the SlickNess-Black has a softer panel shading for some reason. I wanna maybe release this theme but I'm not sure if I can because its basically other peoples' themes spliced together.

do I just take the Folder and make it into a tar.gz file?

EDIT: i figured it out! I'm gonna attatch my very first theme!!

### Post by maniacmusician on 2008-04-26
> **fedex1993 said:**
> where did you get all your backgrounds out they look very nice and there the perfect size for my lappy and my desky

I've gathered most of them from interfacelift, a couple of other sites, and P2P sources. I mainly collect wallpapers in 1680x1050, the resolution of my desktop, because they can also scale down to my laptop, which is also widescreen. The folder in the picture was just a temporary one I put together and threw some images into, for the sake of not exposing too much of my personal hard drive (since my wallpapers are actually quite deep inside the folder heirarchy).

As a gift, here are the wallpapers I use on a regular basis. I've attempted to organize them, but some of the categorizations are a little off, so sorry about that. But since they're the perfect resolution for you, I'm sure you'll enjoy them nonetheless. :)

It's kind of big (85 MB), so I had to put it on mediafire. [http://www.mediafire.com/?gsgnv0y1dxx](http://www.mediafire.com/?gsgnv0y1dxx)

### Post by ph1 on 2008-04-28
> **fedex1993 said:**
> okay i love your calander on the side my question is there anyway that i can get your conky config and any scripts that go with it

Hey fedex1993,

I'm posting my .conkyrc and the scripts I use, as well as some other parts of my .conkyrc that I set up but don't use anymore (in conkyrcalternate).  I think there are probably better scripts out there to do the weather (especially since I don't speak a word of polish, but I'm using a polish script from gnome-look.org), but this works, so don't fix it if it ain't broke, right?

What you will need:
1. sudo apt-get install lm-sensors, hddtemp
2. I also have an nvidia card, so sudo apt-get install nvidia-settings
3. Fonts:  just google these, you can find them for free: Weather, Styelbats, Xspiralmental, Pizzadude Bullets, Deja Vu Sans
4. The scripts: just check to see if the file paths inside the scripts match--you may need to change them.  Also, you'll need to change the kod= line in the weather script (it's polish, called pogodynka) to match your zip code or international code.

PM me if you need any more info on how I got it set up.

Enjoy!

---

### Post by tgm4883 on 2008-04-28
Note about my Desktop.  The AWN bar at the bottom auto hides and get covered by open windows.  The top panel auto hides and when hidden takes 0 pixels.  This allows programs to use the full screen when maximized.  I have the whole procedure documented on [my website]("http://linux.weilandhomes.com/freshsetup") so I can easily set it up the same way for reinstalls.

Icons:  Standard
Theme:  Standard
Background:  xplanet

:EDIT:

I probably won't check this thread too often, so if you have any questions pm me.

### Post by Lostincyberspace on 2008-04-29
How do you have nautilus set up?
I love the big icons with the name and # of file beneath.

---

### Post by SomeGuyDude on 2008-04-29
> **Lostincyberspace said:**
> How do you have nautilus set up?
I love the big icons with the name and # of file beneath.

Well Hardy seems to do the # thing by itself. What I did was I had to manually set each folder to the image (right click on a folder, hit "properties", then click on the little picture at the top left), and fortunately B&W2Style has a lot of them set under scalable>places>256. Then for the size, I just cranked it to 200% for my home folder.

---

### Post by shearn89 on 2008-04-29

nice - wall?

> **Nem1976 said:**
> Anyone know how to change the foot icon?  I have an ubuntu one I want to use but I can't figure out how to change it.

> **Vansinnesvisan said:**
> I *think* it can replaced with "use_custom_icon" in the Configuration Editor under apps->panel->objects->object_#. Maybe replace it with a transparent png to get rid of it entirely. Or change the original icon in usr/share/icons or usr/share/pixmaps, I believe.
